    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_60add301-975f-42b2-8a57-b647204ad7b7'

<span id="freeTextContainer18355326460134178893">Alyssa Gardner hears the whispers of bugs and flowers—precisely the affliction that landed her mother in a mental hospital years before. This family curse stretches back to her ancestor Alice Liddell, the real-life inspiration for Lewis Carroll’s <i>Alice’s Adventures in Wonderland</i>. Alyssa might be crazy, but she manages to keep it together. For now.<br/><br/>When her mother’s mental h</span>
  <span id="freeText18355326460134178893" style="display:none">Alyssa Gardner hears the whispers of bugs and flowers—precisely the affliction that landed her mother in a mental hospital years before. This family curse stretches back to her ancestor Alice Liddell, the real-life inspiration for Lewis Carroll’s <i>Alice’s Adventures in Wonderland</i>. Alyssa might be crazy, but she manages to keep it together. For now.<br /><br />When her mother’s mental health takes a turn for the worse, Alyssa learns that what she thought was fiction is based in terrifying reality. The real Wonderland is a place far darker and more twisted than Lewis Carroll ever let on. There, Alyssa must pass a series of tests, including draining an ocean of Alice’s tears, waking the slumbering tea party, and subduing a vicious bandersnatch, to fix Alice’s mistakes and save her family. She must also decide whom to trust: Jeb, her gorgeous best friend and secret crush, or the sexy but suspicious Morpheus, her guide through Wonderland, who may have dark motives of his own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18355326460134178893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/35547783-kerry-saltvick"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1412235053i/35547783._UX100_CR0,4,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/35547783-kerry-saltvick">Kerry Saltvick</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">While there is nothing extremely graphic, there is sexual innuendo, and soft-core kissing. The kissing is often described in very sensual imagery. Als<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">While there is nothing extremely graphic, there is sexual innuendo, and soft-core kissing. The kissing is often described in very sensual imagery. Also the main character is 15, (16?) So just a few years older than an 8th grader.<br /><br />I would allow my 8th grade year old self to read it, because I knew about the birds and bees already and was mature enough to handle it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_796883722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/796883722" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/796883722?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer796883722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6500195088531831597"><b>This book literally made my jaw drop</b>. I'm still reeling from some of the offensive, annoying and downright incorrect things that made it past editors, proofreaders and buyers.<br/><br/>I could point out the way mental illness is sensationalized for a bit of drama and Alyssa's mother is just put in a straitjacket and wheeled off to a padded cell, even though straitjackets and padded cells haven't been used much since the introduction of psychotropic drugs in the 1950s and especially not for someone in her </span>
  <span id="freeText6500195088531831597" style="display:none"><b>This book literally made my jaw drop</b>. I'm still reeling from some of the offensive, annoying and downright incorrect things that made it past editors, proofreaders and buyers.<br /><br />I could point out the way mental illness is sensationalized for a bit of drama and Alyssa's mother is just put in a straitjacket and wheeled off to a padded cell, even though straitjackets and padded cells haven't been used much since the introduction of psychotropic drugs in the 1950s and especially not for someone in her condition.<br /><br />Or I could talk about the ridiculous YA tropes this book is drowning in. Mary Sue emo girl with plaid tights and dreadlocks lusts after a beautiful control-freak boy who has a girlfriend who is a stunning model, characterized by her short clothing and sexuality and - you guessed it - is a total bitch to the MC for no good reason. Probably because the author needs you to think the evil bitch deserves it when Mary Sue wins the guy.<br /><br />And lets talk about Jeb and Alyssa, shall we? And the fact that this is an actual conversation that takes place in the book:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Al.” His Adam’s apple moves as he swallows. “I want you to put a stop to this Hitch thing. Whatever’s going on, it’s not worth…” He pauses. “Losing an important part of you.”<br />Unbelievable. He thinks I’m such a prude, he won’t even say the word. “You mean my virginity?”<br />His neck flashes red. “You deserve better than some one-night thing. You’re the kind of girl who should have a commitment from a guy who actually cares. Okay?”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>OH MY GOD. Is this real?</b> Not only does this macho asshole think he can tell Alyssa to stop her relationship, but virginity is "an important part of you"? What freaking century am I in? If it wasn't for the iPods, I actually would have thought I'd picked up some historical fiction. I honestly thought we were starting to move on from the days when we gave our teen girls pro-virginity, woman-shaming propaganda. Guess not.<br /><br />Jeb is constantly aggressive and condescending towards Alyssa and it only gets worse when they land themselves in Wonderland. He talks to her like she's five years old and literally pushes her around:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“No.” Jeb crosses my arms over my chest, then lifts me against one of the curtains on the wall so my feet dangle, pinning me like a butterfly to a cork board. “We’re not going anywhere.”</i>
</blockquote><br />And people like this guy! He's supposed to be one of the love interests but he made me furious. <br /><br />Despite the fact that Jeb is an abusive piece of shit, Alyssa still crushes on him throughout the book (blushing as she does it, of course, so you don't mistake her for one of those evil slutty girls). She also has no positive relationships with any other female character, except her coworker who she talks to, like, once.<br /><br />As for the <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> retelling aspect, the book reintroduces many things seen before - talking flowers, drinks/cake making you smaller/bigger, a sort of white rabbit, etc. - and really the only interesting new thing is love interest #2 - Morpheus. Who is, by far, the most interesting thing about this book. In fact, he's the only remotely interesting thing in the book.<br /><br />But even Morpheus isn't enough to convince me to force myself through the second book.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6500195088531831597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1194661824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1194661824" />
    <a title="Kiki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki"><img alt="Kiki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545082712p2/4074594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1194661824?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiki" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki">Kiki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=mayhem-and-misogyny">mayhem-and-misogyny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=lost-the-will-to-live">lost-the-will-to-live</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=love-stinks">love-stinks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=books-to-use-as-weapons">books-to-use-as-weapons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=what-has-been-seen-cannot-be-unseen">what-has-been-seen-cannot-be-unseen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=lolwut">lolwut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=choking-noises">choking-noises</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194661824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5975090116681354903">White girl anthem time, because literally, ew, I can't.<br/><br/>Literally.<br/><br/>Ew.<br/><br/>I can't.<br/><br/>So the other day I was watching Grey's Anatomy and I knew I was making a mistake because, being a casual viewer (and by casual I mean that I can stomach perhaps one episode every seven months) I wasn't invested enough in the convoluted story or the characters to ignore all of the insanely far-fetched medical and social oversights: a woman is furious that her brother died because "I'm a neurosurgeon, and I could have save</span>
  <span id="freeText5975090116681354903" style="display:none">White girl anthem time, because literally, ew, I can't.<br /><br />Literally.<br /><br />Ew.<br /><br />I can't.<br /><br />So the other day I was watching Grey's Anatomy and I knew I was making a mistake because, being a casual viewer (and by casual I mean that I can stomach perhaps one episode every seven months) I wasn't invested enough in the convoluted story or the characters to ignore all of the insanely far-fetched medical and social oversights: a woman is furious that her brother died because "I'm a neurosurgeon, and I could have saved him!" even though by law you cannot operate on your own family; a woman with a broken neck giving birth in an elevator, with no spinal block or stabilizing equipment save for a flimsy neck brace, being told to "stay very still, or your neck will break more!"; a woman who <i>just</i> turned the machines off on her brain-dead husband being back at work after like two days on bereavement leave; the chief of surgery planning to marry the owner of the hospital and then, after one fight, calling off the wedding; surgeons walking around the hospital in gowns and masks and gloves, eating food; surgeons at the ambulance bay with long flowing hair left loose; a man being surprised that his wife has changed after a stint performing life-saving surgery in a war-zone; and a pair of interns left alone with a pregnant woman with a broken neck and subsequently nearly killing her by loosening her neck brace.<br /><br />The list goes on. And it reminds me of this book and the absolutely absurd way it plays out even just from a medical angle. A nurse carries a syringe full of drugs in her pocket; a woman is put in a strait jacket in a padded cell; a young woman with a family is locked away on a ward indefinitely with only scheduled visits.<br /><br />The nurse with the syringe in her pocket? What the fuck. Struck off. You cannot carry drugs around like keys. Even worse is that strait jackets and particularly padded cells are scaremongering horror fiction: using strait jackets, or indeed any extreme physical force, is these days widely considered a breach of human rights. There is no if, and or but - the author was sensationalizing mental illness. A patient like Alyssa's mother would never ever be confined to a strait jacket and certainly not a padded cell.<br /><br />Alison would be assessed, medicated, and put back out into the community. Probably with home help. She's a young woman capable of looking after herself. Gone are the days in which mentally ill people were immediately holed up behind bars. But that's not tantalizing enough, is it, A. G. Howard? That's not sensational or exciting. It's not thrilling to see someone with mental illness take her medicine and live a normal life. <br /><br />This book is FUBAR in terms of how it deals with mental illness. Like holy fuck, I cannot get over the nurse with the syringe in her pocket. Her POCKET! That shit stays on the drug trolley and then goes straight in the goddamn sharps bin when it's done. How did nobody catch this? How? This book went through an agent, an editor, and a whole publishing house, and no one thought to themselves, "Is that even allowed?"<br /><br />Look, I should have known before I even started this. The blurb sort of piqued my interest, because I love parallel universes and girls who fall into them, but <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> always just stank to me. I never liked it. I don't even like the Disney movie and I literally like all of the Disney movies. <br /><br />I guess I thought a retelling would bring something other than fishnets, fuckboys, and sensationalised mental illness to the table. Oh, how wrong I was.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5975090116681354903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_270450707" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270450707" />
    <a title="Melissa Marr" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1971192-melissa-marr"><img alt="Melissa Marr" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556828693p2/1971192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270450707?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa Marr" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa Marr" href="/user/show/1971192-melissa-marr">Melissa Marr</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270450707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10977255032266393530">I LOVED this book enough that I'm posting my first ever detailed Goodreads review. <br/><br/>The writing is gorgeous--lyrical and evocative without ever descending into unnecessarily purple. The story is compelling (& the twist was unexpected), and the characters felt like they were real enough to have heartbeats. The author is also one of those wonderful creatures whose pre-finished books are clean enough to read. I read this in manuscript, pre-galleys, and the writing was so polished that I only noticed</span>
  <span id="freeText10977255032266393530" style="display:none">I LOVED this book enough that I'm posting my first ever detailed Goodreads review. <br /><br />The writing is gorgeous--lyrical and evocative without ever descending into unnecessarily purple. The story is compelling (&amp; the twist was unexpected), and the characters felt like they were real enough to have heartbeats. The author is also one of those wonderful creatures whose pre-finished books are clean enough to read. I read this in manuscript, pre-galleys, and the writing was so polished that I only noticed one error in the text. THAT is rare.<br /><br />SPLINTERED is a great companion read to Carroll's ALICE IN WONDERLAND without disrespecting the original text in any way. It's not a re-telling/re-envisioning, but a story that uses ALICE as background to jump off into a new story. Honestly, I was hesitant to read it because of the ALICE association. (I am a lifelong ALICE fan and former university lit instructor.) However, in A.G. Howard's hands, the allusions to the original story are treated with respect. It was masterfully done. <br /><br />It's also the first book I've read that I could say was actually a read-alike for my Wicked Lovely series. I've seen that phrase thrown around by publishers since WL released, and I usually roll my eyes. SPLINTERED, however, is a perfect fit for any of you who enjoyed WL. In it you will find a pierced artist who is the protag's best friend, a girl who has a major secret and ends up caught up in the politics of a strange world filled with beautiful terrifying creatures. There's even a "living ivy vine" moment. It's a read-alike without being derivative.<br /><br />Most of all, though, SPLINTERED is simply a delicious, disturbing, mad, wonderful read. I can't recommend it highly enough. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10977255032266393530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_513062813" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/513062813" />
    <a title="Demi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4618401-demi"><img alt="Demi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485230309p2/4618401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513062813?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Demi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Demi" href="/user/show/4618401-demi">Demi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4618401-demi?shelf=forced-romance">forced-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4618401-demi?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4618401-demi?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4618401-demi?shelf=gross-mysogyny-warning">gross-mysogyny-warning</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513062813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9095595035156971532">Can we take one moment and wonder how much better this book would have been if Jeb wasn't in it? CAN WE?!<br/><br/>This guy was a major douchebag! Besides the fact that he was as good as useless to the entire plot, he had no respect all for Alyssa's opinions or decisions. "Jeb, I think--" "Shut the fuck up. I decide what you can and can't do."<br/><br/>Protective was not even how I would describe him. Controlling is still an understatement. He treated her like a fucking puppy. Its not even like I'm reading too much</span>
  <span id="freeText9095595035156971532" style="display:none">Can we take one moment and wonder how much better this book would have been if Jeb wasn't in it? CAN WE?!<br /><br />This guy was a major douchebag! Besides the fact that he was as good as useless to the entire plot, he had no respect all for Alyssa's opinions or decisions. "Jeb, I think--" "Shut the fuck up. I decide what you can and can't do."<br /><br />Protective was not even how I would describe him. Controlling is still an understatement. He treated her like a fucking puppy. Its not even like I'm reading too much into this because Morpheus kept pointing it out. And I feel so sorry for his actual girlfriend who he used and cheated on. What the fuck is wrong with his mindset?<br /><br />Alyssa fell into his bullshit everytime. I can't...I just can't even with her. She was a complete mary sue. That's all I have to say.<br /><br />Morpheus had his bullshit detector on the entire time which made me love him. His relationship with Alyssa though was so back and forth it made my head spin.<br /><br />The plot itself was alright. I would give it a 4. The ending was kind of quick and cheapened. <br /><br />Just no with Jeb though. Just no.<br /><br /><br />ETA:<br />A month ago a made the mistake of taking the plunge and reading the sequel (got it from the library no way in hell would I spend money on that trash) and it was even worse than I expected. If you're interested in seeing a (slightly spoilery) rant regarding the sequel and Jeb (again) then you can see it <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/975961045" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br />All I can say is apparently the author based Jeb off of her own husband and if that doesn't make you question the society we live in than I don't know what ever will. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9095595035156971532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1814053904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7449809982211596765">Sometime during summer, I took this book in my hands, looked at it lovingly, and sighed before opening the first page and starting my reading of it.<br/><br/>Oh, it so isn’t the dark but magical story I anticipated. It’s been months since I’ve put it aside to rot next to other books waiting for my interest to rekindle, but I just think that will never happen, because the only thing I like about it is MORPHEUS. <br/><br/>So DNF for now (and probably for ever). Oh well, happily never after. <br/></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1068681335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17305905393499978399">SPOILER FREE REVIEW: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jN6NGkE5uk0'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jN6NG...</a><br/><br/>4.5*<br/><br/><i>“You understand the logic behind the illogical, Alyssa. It's in your nature to find tranquility amid the madness. And that's what we're doing here. We are giving our food a fighting chance.”</i><br/><br/>I knew going into this book that I would either love it or hate it and to be honest, I more so expected the latter. Through the Looking Glass is one of my favourite books and as such I knew I would be drawing comparisons the whole time. Lucky fo</span>
  <span id="freeText17305905393499978399" style="display:none">SPOILER FREE REVIEW: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jN6NGkE5uk0">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jN6NG...</a><br /><br />4.5*<br /><br /><i>“You understand the logic behind the illogical, Alyssa. It's in your nature to find tranquility amid the madness. And that's what we're doing here. We are giving our food a fighting chance.”</i><br /><br />I knew going into this book that I would either love it or hate it and to be honest, I more so expected the latter. Through the Looking Glass is one of my favourite books and as such I knew I would be drawing comparisons the whole time. Lucky for me, I loved this book. <br /><br />I had heard this described as a retelling of Alice's Adventures in Wonderland but I think it is more so a reimagining of Alice's Wonderland, a darker, much more sinister Tim Burton-esque Wonderland. I also found the events of the story aligned much more with Through the Looking Glass than they did with Wonderland, which got kind of confusing for spoilery reasons. Because of this, the book really wasn't what I was expecting, but I mean that in the best possible way.<br /></span>

    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of retellings and Alice in Wonderland</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=dat-cover-yo">dat-cover-yo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=e-arc">e-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=original-and-creative">original-and-creative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=amulet">amulet</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257912583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15616941589186414358"><br/>More of a 3.5 star rating.<br/><br/>Okay, so here is a little truth for you: There is no other children's tale that scared me most as a child than <em>Alice in Wonderland.*</em> I will never forget the first time I heard the story. It was by way of my grandmother and these cassette tapes she bought me called <em>Porch Swing Stories.</em> It was very generous of her, but let me tell you, those tapes were the devil. Pretty much all of the stories were purposefully cranked up in the creepy department and I'm convinced that th</span>
  <span id="freeText15616941589186414358" style="display:none"><br>More of a 3.5 star rating.<br><br>Okay, so here is a little truth for you: There is no other children's tale that scared me most as a child than <em>Alice in Wonderland.*</em> I will never forget the first time I heard the story. It was by way of my grandmother and these cassette tapes she bought me called <em>Porch Swing Stories.</em> It was very generous of her, but let me tell you, those tapes were the devil. Pretty much all of the stories were purposefully cranked up in the creepy department and I'm convinced that the person who created such torture devices never interacted with a child. Later, I saw the Disney movie version of the tale and was further traumatized by the damn Cheshire Cat, who was just a little too happy for my taste, and his Wonderland posse. I mean, what was their problem anyway?<br><p>
  <img alt="alice-in-wonderland-cheshire-cat-disney-movie-pink-walt-disney-Favim.com-43752" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380366714i/719017.jpg" width="350" height="267" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br><p>
  <em>Well, I guess that explains it...</em>
</p><br>Obviously, since losing my heart and soul (as Kat frequently reminds me), being afraid of <em>Alice in Wonderland</em> is no longer an issue for me. But besides that less than disturbing fact, I had to read <em>Splintered</em> because A) The cover is to die for B) The cover is to die for C) The cover is to die for. This level of novel vetting always works for me. That is, except when it doesn't, but that's besides the point. <em>Splintered</em> brings such a unique spin on <em>Alice in Wonderland</em> with rich world building, re-imagined characters and a clever plot.<br><br>Alyssa Gardener, our protagonist, has a family history of insane women all starting with Alice Liddell. In fact, even her very own mother, who she distantly refers to as Allison, is committed to an asylum. With her strange ability to hear the whispers of flowers and bugs, Alyssa fears she is soon to follow. However, her true fear is ultimately losing her mother to the madness unless she can somehow break the Liddell curse. So she gathers family trinkets (a key, mirror, gloves, hair pin, etc.), repeats history and travels down the rabbit hole only to find it's not exactly the same Wonderland described in the famous story.<br><br>If you are one who, unlike myself, knows the original <em>Alice in Wonderland</em> pretty well, then I think you'll be very pleased with what <em>Splintered</em> has to offer. Right from the beginning when we are introduced to Alyssa Gardener, I could see the subtle references. But, of course, simply mentioning pieces of the original isn't enough to make it feel authentic. There's the vivid descriptions, character mannerisms and, of course, Wonderland-like puzzles and riddles. And that is where I think Howard truly excelled with this novel. She effortlessly wove in the old with the new. So instead of it feeling like a simple retelling, it's more along the lines of an <em>extension</em> of the original because it's clear that Howard left no stone unturned when it came to crafting the her Wonderland.<br><br>If that isn't enough to entice you, there's also this gothic feel the novel carries, especially in the beginning when the mystery of Alyssa's past is at it's strongest. Alyssa the skater girl, who likes to wear colored dreds and collects moths for artistic collages. Little things like that added a certain level of charm, but also helped <em>Splintered</em> to stand out as taking a slightly different route as a retelling.<br><br>Now, while I've been singing praises left and right about Splintered, there are a few things that bothered me. However, I should note that it did not detract from my personal enjoyment from the novel much.<br><br><strong>The Characters:</strong><br><br>My biggest problem would have to be Jeb, Alyssa's best friend. I can understand what Howard was going for with his characterization. Present the reader with a character who has to have some type of control over the main character to help show her resulting personal growth by the end of the novel. At least, that's what I got from it. Unfortunately, this did not work out for me. Why? Because 90% of the time I found Jeb to be a controlling douche. In the beginning, Alyssa wants to go to London to study art, so her dad and Jeb sit down for dinner to decide if she can go. Did I mention that he is only a year older than her and the love interest of the story? Yeah... I wasn't exactly thrilled with him having so much say in the matter. Yet, I tried to like Jeb. Tried and failed. Every time he went missing from the storyline, I felt myself really enjoying the book, but when he returned? Nosedive. By the end of the book, the only way to describe how I felt for him is to simply say I tolerated him. Basically, I went from stabby feelings to an eye roll whenever his character had dialogue.<br><br>Even still was his girlfriend, who has a history of bullying Alyssa. Jeb seems to never defend his best friend, but instead expects Alyssa to try harder with getting along. &gt;_&gt; What's worse is that Alyssa never really calls him on that. Why should Alyssa have to place nice with a bully? More importantly, why would her best friend ask that of her and never say anything to his girlfriend?<br><br>The good thing is that once Alyssa got to Wonderland the annoyances decreased significantly. Alyssa's characterization picks up and we are introduced to Morpheus. And this might surprise some that know my tastes, but I kinda liked the guy. I think his twisted personality fit in perfectly with Wonderland. But I do think the reason why he didn't bother me is because I never truly saw him as a contender for Alyssa's heart. I saw that he had feelings for her and that they shared a connection, but I never thought it would go further than that.<br><br>Overall, if you are looking for a richly imagined retelling of <em>Alice in Wonderland,</em> <em>Splintered</em> is definitely the way to go. I had a few mild reservations, but I think most people will probably enjoy seeing just how deep the rabbit hole truly goes. I did and I can't wait to see what future works Howard has planned.<br><br><em>*Hopefully I didn't lose too many cool points with you for that strange, compulsive confession.</em><br><br><em>ARC was received from the publisher via NetGalley for an honest review. Thank you!</em><br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15616941589186414358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_498516815" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/498516815" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/498516815?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer498516815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17809744174409519304">Before I start: how gorgeous is that cover? I mean really, if there exists such a thing as judging a book by its cover, <i>I'm <b>so</b> there</i>.<br/><br/>Alyssa is a descendant of the original Alice Liddell, the inspiration for Lewis Carroll's Alice in Wonderland book. The women in her family suffer from a curse of madness, even the illegitimate by-blows of the family become stricken with insanity after they reach puberty. Her mother ends up in a mental asylum after trying to kill Alyssa when she was a small child, </span>
  <span id="freeText17809744174409519304" style="display:none">Before I start: how gorgeous is that cover? I mean really, if there exists such a thing as judging a book by its cover, <i>I'm <b>so</b> there</i>.<br /><br />Alyssa is a descendant of the original Alice Liddell, the inspiration for Lewis Carroll's Alice in Wonderland book. The women in her family suffer from a curse of madness, even the illegitimate by-blows of the family become stricken with insanity after they reach puberty. Her mother ends up in a mental asylum after trying to kill Alyssa when she was a small child, she and her father both suffer knowing Alison is mad; her father because he still deeply loves his wife, and Alyssa because she knows she is doomed to the same fate. They often visit her mother in the asylum, even if each visit is painful to them both, seeing their loved one in the grips of madness.<br /><br />Alyssa has a close friend, Jeb, who is dating Taelor (I hate her already just by her name), the stereotypical beautiful, spoiled rich girl nemesis. Alyssa has been an outcast in school her entire life ever since Taelor reveals that Alyssa is descended from Alice Liddell. She is subsequently bullied and ridiculed by the other kids for her connection to the Alice of yore. I don't really understand the grounds for this: being related to the original Alice...that's pretty awesome. I would say it's more of a claim to fame, particularly in grade school, rather than anything over which to be ostracized.<br /><br />Alyssa rebels by becoming a skater, wearing as much makeup, hair dye, and dreadlocks as possible to disguise who she really is (the fact that Jeb calls her "Skater Girl" really gives me Avril Lavigne vibes). When the latest visit to her mother in the asylum turns violent, her father is desperate enough to resort to consent to electroconvulsive therapy, Alyssa tries to save her mother by turning to the mysterious boy in her believed hallucinations. She finds herself down the rabbit hole in a darker version of Wonderland, and is accidentally joined by a stubborn and reluctant Jeb. In Wonderland, she meets the boy of whom she dreams, Morpheus, who has appeared in her dreams since she was a child. He tells her to go on a series of quests to fulfill her mission in order to save her mother.<br /><br />The creatures she encounters along the way are definitely based upon the original <i>Alice</i> books, albeit remarkably more twisted. The recent adaptation of <i>Alice</i> by Tim Burton has got <i>nothing</i> on the creepiness of the creatures in this book. I love the clever spin and connection of the original tale with the methods that Alyssa uses to resolve through the dangers she encounters along the way.<br /><br />I love the portrayal of mental illness, and the heroine is someone I actually like, despite my mental image of her being Avril Lavigne. I find it so hard to <i>like</i> most characters in YA novels; most of them are either too damn stubborn (coming from the cut-off-your-nose-to-spite-your-face school), too annoying and contrary, or just plain TSTL. I am happy to say that Alyssa is neither. She is smart, thoughtful, intelligent, and can figure shit out for herself.<br /><br />I disliked the main love interest. Jeb doesn't seem good enough for her; he is overbearing, overprotective, and is the type who denies his own feelings FOR HER SAKE. No thank you, that's not my definition of love. I just wanted to smack Jeb away and leave Alyssa alone to do her thing, because frankly, she repeatedly demonstrates a capability of managing on her own.<br /><br />The plot was great in the beginning, but drifts off in a myriad of confusion in the latter third of the book. The plot became confusing to me, twisting more and more until I didn't really understand what was going on anymore. By the end, I still wasn't sure what happened to resolve the plot. The confusing latter plot and messy ending was my reason for taking off a star, otherwise, it was a beautiful, surreal, fantastically imaginative read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17809744174409519304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2360246674" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2360246674" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2360246674?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781620647257" href="/book/show/18278002-splintered">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2360246674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16192832141096529855"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528735591ra/25721406.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i> “He starts to hum, a haunting melody. No words ride the music, only the familiar notes of a forgotten song.” </i><br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>When I was little I could never quite decide which fairy tale was my favorite. <br/>But the older I was, the more I was fascinated by Alice and her adventure in wonderland. <br/>The thing I liked the most of it? The craziness, the insane and illogical things in it. And the huge amount of fantasy for creating a world like this. <br/>But I always felt like the story was too childish, too </span>
  <span id="freeText16192832141096529855" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528735591ra/25721406.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> “He starts to hum, a haunting melody. No words ride the music, only the familiar notes of a forgotten song.” </i><br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>When I was little I could never quite decide which fairy tale was my favorite. <br>But the older I was, the more I was fascinated by Alice and her adventure in wonderland. <br>The thing I liked the most of it? The craziness, the insane and illogical things in it. And the huge amount of fantasy for creating a world like this. <br>But I always felt like the story was too childish, too naive and nice. <br>So this book was the perfect match for me.<br>In German it’s called “dark wonderland” and finishing this book in just a few days, I can only agree to that. <br>The main character is Alyssa, a young girl with huge artistic talent and whose mother is in a asylum. Soon she finds out that to save her mother from an electric damage, she needs to find the rabbit hole. <br>And soon a huge adventure starts for Al with new friends, enemies and revelations about herself. <br>All in all I think this book was awesome in its storytelling. The twists and turns and all the fantasy in it is hugely entertaining and fascinating. <br>I loved it, especially all the plot twists that make me greedy for more. More insane thoughts and people and more creepy but fantastic creations. <br><br>Character ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br><i> “No one knows what he or she is capable of until things are at their darkest.” </i><br>I think this part of the book has a few flaws and weaknesses. <br>Starting with our main character Alyssa whose really brave, smart and all In really likable. But being around Jeb she always lets herself be saved. She’s playing the weak link and lets him speak for her. <br>In general she’s not deciding things for herself, always listening to some boys who try to push her to their side. <br>In the end that changes, but still, it’s a bit annoying that even though she could’ve easily saved her a lot of trouble and emotions by going through her adventure alone, she still chose to be guided by her all time hero Jeb. <br>Okay. Lets be honest. I hated Jeb. Didn’t start liking him throughout the book, even though I maybe should have. I just couldn’t. <br>He always spoke for her and decided for her, even though she could’ve easily done it herself. But no, he needed to play her hero and savior all the time. I know some girls and boys love this, but I think a good mixture or balance of strong woman who can save the world herself and men who support her and save her when all is lost and she really needs his help, is the best. <br>Morpheus was a really interesting character that sometimes reminded me of Rhys from acowar, but in a more wicked way. <br>He was extremely selfish with a huge intelligence and a great self-confidence. <br>He is a real good tactician that can master a plan easily even though people get hurt or killed. I liked that about him - the ruthlessness in his character. <br>All in all I think Morpheus was the most interesting of them and I’m glad we get to see a lot of him in the book.<br><br>World ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br><i> “Little blossom in peach and red<br>Trapping boys with your pretty head;<br>Tease and play, be coy and smart<br>For you will one day break his heart” </i><br>All the points for the world building in this book. The landscape, the creations, the people, twist and turns. It was brilliant even though it had many inspirations by Alice in wonderland. But that’s what I liked about it. It was like a really dark twisted and creepy wonderland with similar characters but a really great storyline. <br><br>Relationships ⭐️<br><i> “You can put me down now," I grump.<br>"I don't know. It's a lot easier to save your ass when I have it riding on my shoulder. </i><br>Oh wow. I never had this situation. Every time a book had a love triangle, throughout the book I choose one side - and then I was team XY for the whole trilogy. <br>But in this book... I didn’t choose a side. <br>I didn’t like either of them. I couldn’t stand Jeb because of his character and I didn’t like Morpheus because even though he was really interesting, he really hurt Alyssa in a really bad and horrible way. <br>In my opinion this book could’ve easily live without a stupid love triangle (especially Jeb in it...), because Alyssa is a great female character and could’ve been a huge female hero. <br>But no... always boys that try to guide her on their side. <br>That was literally a part I really hated about the book. It was just unnecessary.<br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Well. Well. Well. This wasn’t a masterpiece of words but it was good. It was fluent and simple with a lot of imaginative descriptions. <br>The twist and turns, revelations and creation made the book so wonderfully individual. <br>So, I definitely recommend this book to anyone who love Alice in Wonderland and wants to try a new, twisted and creepy version of it.<br><br><i> “I need to get to that tea party and wake up the guests."<br>Jeb looks at me. "And how are you supposed to do that? Give a magical kiss to the half-baked hatmaker?” </i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528735591ra/25721407.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16192832141096529855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_409230179" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/409230179" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/409230179?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer409230179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9084980903658202102">Splintered seems to be another instance where I appear as the black sheep. I've seen numerous positive reviews of the novel before I went into it, and came out feeling pretty disappointed. A book I even thought at first I would absolutely love, ended up being just a little too drawn out. I had little love for the characters, and the fascinating twists came a little too late to grab a higher rating.<br/><br/>I will say, the novel is not a complete let-down, especially for Alice in Wonderland fans. I, mysel</span>
  <span id="freeText9084980903658202102" style="display:none">Splintered seems to be another instance where I appear as the black sheep. I've seen numerous positive reviews of the novel before I went into it, and came out feeling pretty disappointed. A book I even thought at first I would absolutely love, ended up being just a little too drawn out. I had little love for the characters, and the fascinating twists came a little too late to grab a higher rating.<br><br>I will say, the novel is not a complete let-down, especially for Alice in Wonderland fans. I, myself, have never been a junkie of classic fairy tales, but out of all, Alice remains one of my favorites. Thus, I was instantly taken by the plot in Splintered. It has great connections to the Alice story we've known for years, taking us into the lives of Alice's very own great-great-granddaughter--Alyssa. By 20%, I was fully enraptured in this tale by which time I had incredibly high hopes for, thinking it a for sure winner. Sadly, when the initial high of this exciting plot peaks, it quickly crashes into an adventure filled with so many detours and a tiresome love triangle. It made it hard for me to even finish it.<br><br>To draw a picture of this love triangle: we have Jeb, a jerk who Alyssa is head over heals in love with. The boy next door who inadvertently becomes Alyssa's sidekick in this twisted wonderland, Jeb is not likeable at all. Mostly, he's boring, and any personality he does have includes him being irritating in his behaviour towards Alyssa. Sure I've seen worse love interests, he's hardly even in my least favorite, but his character is simply not attractive in the least. His obvious denied love for Alyssa, and their "we love each other but we can't because (insert lame reason here)" relationship is exhausting. Then comes Morpheus, a Wonderland native who is also madly in love with Alyssa and trying to win her over. I actually did not mind him. Sure he's a wanker, but he's abruptly honest about his personality so you can't help but just accept that he is who he is. We're not "supposed" to like him, so, as usual, I loved to hate him. :D<br><br>Honestly, I don't abhor love triangles as much as most, but I need to understand why it exist, and in this case it felt too much like the romance was there just because. It took too much attention off of the plot, which is by far the best modern Alice story I've read. The middle section could have easily been cut in half. Alyssa is taken on so many runarounds without getting any answers that it takes a lot of patience to get through this book. I'm not known for my patience…<br><br>I will have to say, however, that at the end I was thoroughly satisfied with the way the story played out. Cut out the romance, the long winded deviations, a boring protagonist, and we have ourselves a 5-star! (…crickets…) In all honesty, the main plot is fantastic. The plays on the original Alice, and the way the author makes it her own with unique twists is worth the read for that alone! I loved how we get a completely new "no, <i>this</i> is what actually happened" story. It's brilliant! This leads me to recommend this novel to any Alice fan, regardless of my issues with the less endearing parts of this novel. Just, be patient.<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346185i/700655.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9084980903658202102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_262855088" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262855088" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3736122-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524600311p2/3736122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/262855088?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/3736122-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=kindle-books">kindle-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262855088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16562094900364440084">For this review, I will be utilizing the gloriously expressive face of Tom Hiddleston.<br/><br/>To <i>Splintered</i>, I would basically just like to say one thing:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380367509ra/720029.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When I saw the blurb for this book, I was a little unsure. I love Alice in Wonderland (both the book and the Disney movie...along with like, every adaptation there's ever been). But the bit about Alyssa maybe being crazy sounded weird, and I'd also heard some negative things about <i>Alice in Zombieland</i>, so I was sort of wary of any YA take on this classi</span>
  <span id="freeText16562094900364440084" style="display:none">For this review, I will be utilizing the gloriously expressive face of Tom Hiddleston.<br><br>To <i>Splintered</i>, I would basically just like to say one thing:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380367509ra/720029.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When I saw the blurb for this book, I was a little unsure. I love Alice in Wonderland (both the book and the Disney movie...along with like, every adaptation there's ever been). But the bit about Alyssa maybe being crazy sounded weird, and I'd also heard some negative things about <i>Alice in Zombieland</i>, so I was sort of wary of any YA take on this classic.<br><br>Y'all, I'm here to tell you: <b>don't be afraid to read this book!</b> It is wonderful in every way.<br><br>Basically, this book made me feel lots of feels. The good kind.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380367509ra/720030.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is one of those times where I can't find anything to criticize. I liked the heroine, I liked the love interests (yes, TWO!), I liked the pacing and the plot, and I liked the writing style.<br><br>But probably my favorite part of the book was the worldbuilding. Howard takes the original Alice mythology and not only expands on it but also changes it in a lot of ways. This is NOT the Wonderland from Lewis Carroll's children's book; it's darker, more terrifying. But it's still magical and gorgeous, and I kind of wanted to live there despite the scary bits.<br><br>Howard's writing is very visual, conjuring up these great images that really help you share her vision for Wonderland. Everything is described beautifully, and I can't help wishing this could be a movie or TV show or something. I feel like it would be gorgeous.<br><br>Also, this is sort of a small thing, but I loved that the clothes are described so thoroughly. Personally, I'm into fashion. And I love it when our heroine is too. And there are LOTS of cool clothes in this book. Everybody dresses sort of punk/alternative, so that was really fun.<br><br>Now, I MUST gush about the romance.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380367509ra/720031.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Hats off to you, Ms. Howard, for writing not one but two very hot boys. One of which is super creepy but so totally awesome in a scare-the-pants-off-you sort of way. Why is he so awesome? Because he's FREAKING MORPHEUS!<br><br>Now, most of you probably think this when you see the name "Morpheus":<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>The cool people, however, think of this:<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>But in A.G. Howard's book, Morpheus is one very delicious netherling with black wings, a Cockney accent, and a fetish for well-made hats. I loved him. He's the sort of bad boy you love to read about (but totally never want to meet in real life).<br><br>Then there's Jeb, the best-friend-turned-lover type but who's not really the boy next door. He's got lots of issues, but he's not brooding or mean. It was nice reading about a guy who has angst but isn't a douche. Yeah, he was protective, but I didn't think in the cliche, annoying sort of way you find a lot in YA. He was adorable, and while I sometimes wished he could have taken a more active role in the plot (he often plays sidekick to Alyssa - but, hey, this is HER story, not his), I really enjoyed reading the scenes he was in.<br><br><i>Splintered</i> is probably one of the coolest, most imaginative YA books I've ever read. It's a mixture of a lot of my favorite things, and I found it a lot different than other fantasy titles out there. It side-stepped a lot of the cliches, I thought, and the premise is just so incredibly interesting that it was impossible for me to not fall head-over-heels for it.<br><br>This was my first 2013 debut I read, and it was awesome.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380367509ra/720034.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I will most CERTAINLY be reading future books by A.G. Howard!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16562094900364440084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_312561797" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312561797" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3388215-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373331875p2/3388215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/312561797?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/3388215-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312561797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2031528606397828977"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380375077ra/729534.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I sure wish now that I'd taken the blue pill and not read this book...<br/> <br/>On paper, a book might seem like many things. Some might seem like rage-inducing snooze fests directed at sexist people with a death wish. Incredibly epic, of course, is the preferred synopsis of choice. When I picked up SPLINTERED, glossed over the synopsis a few times, and took it in with a final hard look, I saw one word flash across my eyes – AWESOME. And that was what I took when I opened my Kindle and started this one. </span>
  <span id="freeText2031528606397828977" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380375077ra/729534.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I sure wish now that I'd taken the blue pill and not read this book...<br> <br>On paper, a book might seem like many things. Some might seem like rage-inducing snooze fests directed at sexist people with a death wish. Incredibly epic, of course, is the preferred synopsis of choice. When I picked up SPLINTERED, glossed over the synopsis a few times, and took it in with a final hard look, I saw one word flash across my eyes – AWESOME. And that was what I took when I opened my Kindle and started this one. Sometimes, though, a synopsis misleads you. For me, SPLINTERED seemed epic in a Tim Burton-esque way. In reality, it was a one way trip to Hot Topic where they were having a blowout sale on Alice in Wonderland merchandise with Johnny Depp’s face plastered everywhere.<br><br>SPLINTERED is the story of Alyssa, the daughter of a woman afflicted with severe psychiatric issues, and the granddaughter and great-granddaughter of others similarly affected. Alyssa herself can hear bugs and flowers speaking to her. With her love interest Jeb, a brooding artist currently dating the high strung and stereotypical enemy Taelor, Alyssa goes on a hunt to destroy the curse, leading her down the rabbit hole right into Wonderland.<br><br>The first 20% of this book is a tedious exposition on Alyssa’s current life. Her mother is at Soul’s Asylum, where she eats only out of tea cups among other strange things. Alyssa skateboards and listens to music while mooning over artist Jeb, a boy who draws her in his sketchbook and dreams of going to London – on the dime of his girlfriend Taelor’s father, sadly – to start his career. There is a strong focus on the fact he has a garnet-studded labret piercing.<br><br>This was my first warning that I might not like this book. I never was into the goth, emo, Hot Topic-type scene other than secretly listening to Rob Zombie and Marilyn Manson on my iPod occasionally. SPLINTERED’s focus is not so much on a strong, well-plotted story as much as it is on concentrating on imagery that Tim Burton might be proud of if Tim Burton put in fake dreads and made Edward Skateboardhands instead of Scissorhands. SPLINTERED tries too hard to be cool, and loses itself in the process.<br><br>I never connected to any of the characters, including our heroine Alyssa. The rest of the cast became a massive blur punctuated by the occasional strange character that never was developed. By the time the book ended after a meandering course of wild goose chases and strange trips that made no sense, many of the characters became a singular mass of boring and blah. Likewise, the plot was muddled, confusing, and at times the imagery – remarkably well thought out, if a little too obnoxious in the descriptions – became lost in confusing schpiels about mooning and being angry with Jeb and Morpheus, the extremely jerky other love interest/man-moth hybrid thing. I’m still not sure about that.<br><br>SPLINTERED suffers heavily from an over emphasis on the romance and being different and loses itself in the process. We are drawn into a love triangle that I found to be rather unappealing, seeing as how I didn’t like Jeb or Morpheus. In fact, I quite hated Morpheus and didn’t see what Alyssa saw in him other than the moth that she was BFFs with when she was little, which wasn’t creepy at all. Oh, and the psychiatry in this book? It seemed like Tom Cruise at times was lecturing me. I must be glib.<br><br>VERDICT: Sometimes, a book and a reader just don’t mesh. This happened to me with SPLINTERED sadly. Too much romance and not enough plot make Megan a dull girl.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380375077ra/729535.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2031528606397828977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1831380474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1831380474" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1831380474?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1831380474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15502395792685490181">Alyssa is a descendant of Alice Liddell- the Alice who inspired Carroll to write his tale of white rabbits and fantastical creatures. But, Alyssa has a family secret: the women of her bloodline go insane when they come of age.<br/><br/>She tries to look on the positive side of this: <i>"At least one good thing has come out of my inherited insanity. Without the delusions, I might never have found my artistic medium."</i> pg 10, ebook.<br/><br/>Alyssa is in love with Jeb, a dark and brooding young man with a penchant for gr</span>
  <span id="freeText15502395792685490181" style="display:none">Alyssa is a descendant of Alice Liddell- the Alice who inspired Carroll to write his tale of white rabbits and fantastical creatures. But, Alyssa has a family secret: the women of her bloodline go insane when they come of age.<br /><br />She tries to look on the positive side of this: <i>"At least one good thing has come out of my inherited insanity. Without the delusions, I might never have found my artistic medium."</i> pg 10, ebook.<br /><br />Alyssa is in love with Jeb, a dark and brooding young man with a penchant for grunge clothing and a lip piercing (that she talks about all the time). But, he is dating the most popular girl in Alyssa's high school class, Taelor (of course).<br /><br />Things get really exciting when Alyssa starts to hear voices coming from the bugs and plants.<br /><br />After a brief introduction where the reader learns that Jeb is freakishly controlling and Alyssa's mother is in an insane asylum, she falls through a mirror and after some trials, finds her way into Wonderland.<br /><br />I thought this could have been a potentially interesting re-telling of the classic <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> story, but <i>Splintered's</i> uniqueness is stifled under a bunch of teen angst and a love triangle.<br /><br />Granted, I'm not the target audience for this book, but I'd been on a roll lately with awesome fairy tale re-tellings and I thought I'd give it a shot. Oh well.<br /><br />I actually enjoyed A.G. Howard's interpretation of Wonderland itself. The characters were familiar but twisted slightly.<br /><br />Here's a passage from the tea party- my favorite part: <i>"Now we need to get back to our world. Like yesterday." "Yesterday, you say?" the hatmaker warbles in his bouncing timbre. "Yesterday is doable." Guffawing, the hare slaps a knee and adds, "Although two yesterdays would be impossible." The Door Mouse snickers, slipping back into his uniform. "No, no! You can retrogress as many yesterdays as you please. Simply walk backward the rest of your life."</i> pg 187, ebook.<br /><br />Howard nailed the classic characterizations, but Carroll's original creations were far superior to Alyssa, Jeb, and Morpheus, who were her main contributions to the story.<br /><br />Disregard my opinions on this book if you simply must read any and all fairy tale re-tellings because, at the very least, it is that.<br /><br />Just be aware what you're picking up- a young adult romance/coming of age- and if that's what you're in the mood for, you may really enjoy it.<br /><br />I find that my expectations shape my opinion of a book almost as much as the text itself. For example, I think if I had been warned that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11300302.Alice_in_Zombieland__White_Rabbit_Chronicles___1_" title="Alice in Zombieland (White Rabbit Chronicles, #1) by Gena Showalter" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice in Zombieland</a> had really very little to do with the Wonderland story, I may not have disliked it as much as I did.<br /><br /><i>Splintered</i> actually has a lot of the original Wonderland in it and, if I had to choose between <i>Alice in Zombieland</i> or <i>Splintered</i>, I'd pick this in a heartbeat.<br /><br />Some highly recommended horror/fairy tale re-tellings (for adults): <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23398606.Alice__The_Chronicles_of_Alice___1_" title="Alice (The Chronicles of Alice, #1) by Christina Henry" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30462067.All_Darling_Children" title="All Darling Children by Katrina Monroe" rel="nofollow noopener">All Darling Children</a>.<br /><br />Thanks for reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15502395792685490181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
