    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1356894637" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1356894637" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475352701p2/45261627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1356894637?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=kings-and-queens">kings-and-queens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=beware-of-mary-sue">beware-of-mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=gothic-fiction">gothic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=dark-haired-male-entity">dark-haired-male-entity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=fops-and-fools">fops-and-fools</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=the-woods">the-woods</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=because-princesses">because-princesses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=hades-and-persephone">hades-and-persephone</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1356894637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17833666530991556089">A.G. Howard’s <i>Splintered</i> is tied with Tim Burton’s <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> as the best modernized take on Lewis Carroll’s classic that I’ve read, better than Frank Beddor’s <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44170.The_Looking_Glass_Wars__The_Looking_Glass_Wars___1_' title='The Looking Glass Wars (The Looking Glass Wars, #1) by Frank Beddor' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Looking Glass Wars</a>
</i>. That is a very low bar.<br/><br/>Our heroine, who narrates her tale in first-person present-tense, is Alyssa Gardner, the great-great-great-great…granddaughter of Alice Liddell, the inspiration for Carroll’s book. Her heritage is a well-known fact in her hometown, as is the fact that each woman in the family lin</span>
  <span id="freeText17833666530991556089" style="display:none">A.G. Howard’s <i>Splintered</i> is tied with Tim Burton’s <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> as the best modernized take on Lewis Carroll’s classic that I’ve read, better than Frank Beddor’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44170.The_Looking_Glass_Wars__The_Looking_Glass_Wars___1_" title="The Looking Glass Wars (The Looking Glass Wars, #1) by Frank Beddor" rel="nofollow noopener">The Looking Glass Wars</a>
</i>. That is a very low bar.<br><br>Our heroine, who narrates her tale in first-person present-tense, is Alyssa Gardner, the great-great-great-great…granddaughter of Alice Liddell, the inspiration for Carroll’s book. Her heritage is a well-known fact in her hometown, as is the fact that each woman in the family line since the original Alice has lost her mind. (In real life, nothing of the kind happened to Alice. This would hurt me if I were a descendant of hers; it bothers me enough as no relation). The kids in town have always taunted Alyssa about her ancestry, especially since her mom needed to be institutionalized.<br><br>Alyssa’s father is a sweetheart, but utterly clueless. She also has a friend named Jeb, who veers between disinterest in, and creepy flirtation with, Alyssa. Alyssa claims that she’s always had a crush on Jeb (which is obvious) but that he sees her as his little sister (which is never conveyed). Jeb has a sister, who works at the same emo thrift store as Alyssa. <br><br>Luckily for Alyssa, she likes her job, she likes to skateboard, and she likes to stab insects and flowers and glue them onto her paintings, so she has some solace in life. She does not kill the bugs or plants for their own sake, but because she hears them talking to her – the first sign of her hereditary illness. <br><br>A trip to see her mom at the insane asylum – which appears to be frozen in the 1950s – goes so badly that harsh medical treatment (of the kind not seen today) is suggested. Terrified, Alyssa wracks her brain for a way to save her mom, and resurrects some long-forgotten memories, particularly her early childhood adventures with a shape-shifter, sometimes a moth, sometimes a blue-haired boy.<br><br>Sensing this being can help her somehow, Alyssa calls on him, and he appears in her closet mirror.<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524944934ra/25449511.gif" width="500" height="211" alt="POTO Mirror" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This opens a (stupidly complicated) portal to the same rabbit hole the original Alice fell down all those years ago. Unfortunately, she’s been pining over Jeb all evening and her thoughts summon him to her. Together, they venture into Wonderland.<br><br>After facing a number of dangerous creatures – dark versions of the talking flowers from <i>Through the Looking Glass</i> and the Walrus from Tweedledum and Tweedledee’s poem in the same book – and making out despite Jeb having a girlfriend at home – they find their way to the blue-haired, moth-winged young man, Morpheus the Netherling, a sorcerer and a kingmaker. Morpheus is pleased to see Alyssa, but incensed at Jeb tagging along.<br><br>In his creepy palace, Morpheus explains to Alyssa that she is the rightful Queen of Wonderland (somehow) and he wants to crown her and save the kingdom. He might have done a better job explaining if he had stuck to explaining and not spent quite so much time hitting on her.<br><br>He holds a disturbing feast—where the duck entrée is still alive despite being cooked and <i>wants</i> to be eaten—which turns chaotic due to…something (it’s been a few months since I’ve read the book, and the book did not bat a thousand for coherency). Alyssa somehow discovers that Morpheus is in love with the White Queen, who ostensibly died years ago but has survived in a magical box – a Jabberlock. Apparently all his scheming on her behalf was really for the sake of his old darling instead. Feeling betrayed on a number of levels, the girl turns her back on Morpheus and flees with Jeb.<br><br>Alyssa and Jeb traverse Wonderland, meeting strange creatures, kissing, and having stupid arguments because he’s a jealous creep and convinced that something untoward happened between her and Morpheus (never mind him and Taylor back home). <br><br>Eventually (thank God!) they get separated, and Alyssa has to traverse the Wonderland of the Dead on her own, searching for the cure for her mom. Successful, she comes back to Morpheus and reaches a compromise with him. He wants to help her now – he claims he always has – and together they kill a monster. She finds out that Jeb is dead, but wishes to undo the whole adventure and saves him.<br><br>At home, she restores her mother’s sanity, makes peace with Morpheus, confronts Jeb’s cartoon of a girlfriend, and makes out with Jeb himself. The end, for now.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524944934ra/25449508.gif" width="640" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">" width="40" height="100" alt="TSwift YBWM"/&gt;<br><br>As you can see, this book had very little plot. Two characters had a pulse (guess who they were) and the others, one in particular, were dead weight. The heroine’s relationships with her two suitors seemed based entirely on hormones; it seemed that every conversation with either Jeb or Morpheus deteriorated into a make-out session. <br><br>Yet the world-building was actually quite good. Many of Howard’s inventions – such as the Jabberlock – are perfectly Carrollian. She also has a good eye for visuals, and her taste in books and movies is similar to mine. There are plenty of references to <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11260667.The_Phantom_Of_The_Opera" title="The Phantom Of The Opera by Gaston Leroux" rel="nofollow noopener">The Phantom Of The Opera</a>, Labyrinth</i>, and the myth of Hades and Persephone. Morpheus and Alyssa are clearly meant to be such a pair, following the footsteps of Erik and Christine, and Jareth and Sarah. Sometimes they even almost measure up.<br><br>Jeb is supposed to be the Raoul to Morpheus’ Erik, and he is abysmal at it. His only useful quality is his brawn, which comes in handy when facing monsters, but Alyssa is almost always able to save the day herself through magic or charm. Meanwhile, Jeb is possessive, patronizing, and hypocritical – but portrayed as the “nice guy”, the safe Betty to Morpheus’ Veronica. Howard keeps telling us that Jeb and Alyssa have chemistry, but I don’t see it and never did.<br><br>In short, there is no reason for Jeb Holt to exist. Removing him would cut out half the silly make-out scenes, make Alyssa far more developed by forcing her to travel the strange world alone, and free up time for more world-building, an actual plot, and some character development for Morpheus so he doesn’t come across as nothing more than the pale little brother of Erik or Jareth. <i>Labyrinth</i> was just fine without a love triangle.<br><br>The book also comes across as oddly dated, given the Hot Topic imagery found throughout. I am convinced that Morpheus, with his jagged hair, guyliner, and penchant for top hats and cravats, is based on an emo band frontman – Andy Biersack (Black Veil Brides), Bill Kaulitz (Tokio Hotel), Brendon Urie (Panic! at the Disco) and Gerard Way (My Chemical Romance) are all possibilities – and Alyssa, with her long fair hair, heavy makeup, skateboarding, and sass, could not be more clearly patterned on Avril Lavigne. Alas for Howard, she published the book in 2013, and this particular party was pretty much over by 2010, but honestly it does not appear to have hurt her sales.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524944934ra/25449510.gif" width="500" height="260" alt="Brendon" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524944934ra/25449509.gif" width="500" height="240" alt="Avril" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Content Advisory:</b><br><br><i>Violence:</i> There’s the whole horrid scene with the cooked, live meats, where nothing is shown but much is implied. There’s also a fair amount of blood, although little actual death, and still-living severed heads are preserved in a magical box.<br><br><i>Language:</i> I don’t remember any terrible words, but it’s been awhile.<br><br><i>Sex:</i> Lots of kissing, described in great detail. There are points where things could escalate between Alyssa and either boy, but they never do. <br><br><i>Substance Abuse:</i> People ingest alcohol at Morpheus’ feast, and given the subject of the book there’s a few inevitable drug jokes. Pretty mild.<br><br>In conclusion, <i>Splintered</i> is a beautifully printed book, and its prose isn’t bad. It has a lot of potential as a story, too. But Jeb is a simply terrible character, who holds the story back by contributing nothing and forcing a love triangle where it’s not needed. The sequels are worth reading, but they could have been so much better if he just. Didn't. Exist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17833666530991556089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/852434557" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/852434557?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=insta-love-add-water">insta-love-add-water</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bubbling-under-5-stars">bubbling-under-5-stars</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer852434557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8677884005413837924">Splintered reads exactly like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_' title='The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Iron King</a>, except without the awesomeness of Puck and Grimalkin.<br/><br/>Both have incredible world-building. Even me, who has never officially watched Alice in Wonderland (Which come to think of it, is a serious flaw in my Disney education) can see the parallels Howard drew between the original and this wonderful reimagining. Old friends are here: the talking flowers, Cheshire cat, the Caterpillar (I'll get to Morpheus a bit later) and I absolutely loved the concept of </span>
  <span id="freeText8677884005413837924" style="display:none">Splintered reads exactly like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_" title="The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron King</a>, except without the awesomeness of Puck and Grimalkin.<br><br>Both have incredible world-building. Even me, who has never officially watched Alice in Wonderland (Which come to think of it, is a serious flaw in my Disney education) can see the parallels Howard drew between the original and this wonderful reimagining. Old friends are here: the talking flowers, Cheshire cat, the Caterpillar (I'll get to Morpheus a bit later) and I absolutely loved the concept of Alyssa being a descendant of the original Alice.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388297752ra/7791007.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The one thing that irked me were the love interests. Or more specially, a macho dominating asshole by the name of Jeb.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384292994ra/6839215.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I hated him. I hated him. I hated him. He bosses Alyssa around all the time like he's her fucking dad. He orders Al to eat (Hey, look, Edward/Xavier are in Wonderland too!) He thinks the most important part of Al is her <i>virginity. <br><br>"Al." His Adam's apple moves as he swallows. "I want you to put a stop to this Hitch thing. Whatever's going on, it's not worth..." He pauses. "Losing an important part of you."<br><br>Unbelievable. He thinks I'm such a prude, he won't even say the word. "You mean my virginity?"</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393285ra/757162.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because that fucking slip of membrane is <i>so</i> important. Do you want to forbid Ally from riding bikes too, huh, Jeb? That sonofabitch triangular seat is getting hot and cosy with Al's virginity. Are you going to take a sledgehammer to that?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392972471ra/8641333.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He is an absolute jackass and destroyed what should have been an awesome book. And you know what the worst part is—<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm 99.9% sure he's the guy Al is going to choose in the end. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Now onto Morpheus—the other half of the love triangle. (It's not really a spoiler, we all knew there was going to be one) Just as Jeb is cast in the role of the <s>douchebag</s> steadfast best friend, Morpheus is the dark, intriguing stranger who shrouded in secrecy.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392972471ra/8641334.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The thing is, I've never been drawn to the dark, broody types. I prefer <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/47329-the-iron-fey" rel="nofollow noopener">Pucks</a> as opposed to Ashes. But thanks to the utter despicableness of Jeb, I have no choice but to root for him. And honestly, he sort of won me over in the end <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ when he sacrificed himself for Al. How can you not love a guy like that?<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380370424ra/723238.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Plus, he's sexy. 'Nuff said.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392972471ra/8641335.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The other thing that irked me was Alyssa's bone with Taelor. It's like the author wants us to hate her, what with her cool-girl vibes and hippy name. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392972471ra/8641336.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sure, she's dating your best friend aka the guy you like, but that's no reason to be a bitch to her. Or <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[steal her money for that matter <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And you never made a move, so you can't blame her if Taelor swooped in first.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392972471ra/8641337.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, the thing with Jeb <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[dating Taelor so he can forget about Alyssa? <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380909301ra/3179260.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>But despite those pesky problems, Splintered was still a great read and a highly imaginative retelling of <i>Alice in Wonderland</i>. I highly recommend it.<br><br>And, Jeb?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/514224.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah, I just had to do that.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858062116" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of Unhinged</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858072551" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of Ensnared</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223504075" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of Untamed</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1578384376" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1578384376" />
    <a title="Lexy S.C.  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51158653-lexy-s-c"><img alt="Lexy S.C.  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464296959p2/51158653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1578384376?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lexy S.C.  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lexy S.C.  " href="/user/show/51158653-lexy-s-c">Lexy S.C.  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51158653-lexy-s-c?shelf=to-burn">to-burn</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1578384376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9917208709960219804">I have no words to describe how <b>terrible</b> Splintered was. Alice in Wonderland is a childhood favourite of mine, so I had pretty high expectations of Splintered. Unfortunately, I didn't like <s>much</s> anything about it. The plot was overdone. Way overdone. Alice the great-great-grandmother, then Alicia, then Alison, then Alyssa!? That is a bit much, don't you think?<br/>I was expecting a bit more from the plot. A little more substance and a little less...<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466608668i/19499580._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I found the whole thing a bit stupid. And don't even </span>
  <span id="freeText9917208709960219804" style="display:none">I have no words to describe how <b>terrible</b> Splintered was. Alice in Wonderland is a childhood favourite of mine, so I had pretty high expectations of Splintered. Unfortunately, I didn't like <s>much</s> anything about it. The plot was overdone. Way overdone. Alice the great-great-grandmother, then Alicia, then Alison, then Alyssa!? That is a bit much, don't you think?<br>I was expecting a bit more from the plot. A little more substance and a little less...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466608668i/19499580._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I found the whole thing a bit stupid. And don't even get me started on Jeb. Jeez. What a loser. He helped ruin the book for me, among many other things. <br>I almost didn't finish this. It seems to drag on and on, and the version of the book that I read had a PURPLE FONT. Yes, PURPLE. I hate fonts that are not black and normal looking. HATE THEM. It annoyed me the whole way as I struggled through the words.<br>I <s>am sorry to say</s> can honestly say that this was one of the worst books I have read in 2016. Terrible. I've yet to find a fairy-tale retelling I love. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9917208709960219804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1020019693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1020019693" />
    <a title="Vanessa J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j"><img alt="Vanessa J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468102148p2/19590155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1020019693?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa J." href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j">Vanessa J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=love-the-cover">love-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=boo-girl-hate">boo-girl-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=i-want-to-murder-someone">i-want-to-murder-someone</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1020019693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7902944430664862653">I'm gonna be honest with you: <b>I liked Lewis Carroll's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13023.Alice_in_Wonderland__Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland___1_' title='Alice in Wonderland (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland, #1) by Lewis Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alice in Wonderland</a>.</b> It may seem like a bunch of nonsense, but I liked it. And the same can be said about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/83346.Through_the_Looking_Glass__and_What_Alice_Found_There__Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland___2_' title='Through the Looking-Glass, and What Alice Found There (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland, #2) by Lewis Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Through the Looking-Glass, and What Alice Found There</a> - this one being even more nonsense, but the plot was more clever... if something that makes no sense can be clever.<br/><br/>Of course I was gonna go crazy when I saw this was a retelling of that classic (if you don't believe me, just look at the pre-review below, which I wrote like two years a</span>
  <span id="freeText7902944430664862653" style="display:none">I'm gonna be honest with you: <b>I liked Lewis Carroll's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13023.Alice_in_Wonderland__Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland___1_" title="Alice in Wonderland (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland, #1) by Lewis Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice in Wonderland</a>.</b> It may seem like a bunch of nonsense, but I liked it. And the same can be said about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/83346.Through_the_Looking_Glass__and_What_Alice_Found_There__Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland___2_" title="Through the Looking-Glass, and What Alice Found There (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland, #2) by Lewis Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Through the Looking-Glass, and What Alice Found There</a> - this one being even more nonsense, but the plot was more clever... if something that makes no sense can be clever.<br><br>Of course I was gonna go crazy when I saw this was a retelling of that classic (if you don't believe me, just look at the pre-review below, which I wrote like two years ago). Besides, this had all the potential for being a great story. Lovers of Alice and fantasy would find a treat in here. I'm both of those, yet <b>this was completely underwhelming.</b><br><br>But let's get done with the good first, which can be reduced to one thing: The writing. Not over-the-roofs beautiful, but it's descriptive and makes the story flow easily. The author describes in detail how everything looks through the eyes of Alyssa, the subject to a curse that runs in the veins of all the females descendant of Alice Liddell, the inspiration for Carroll's book.<br><br>Everyone in her family has been tagged as crazy ever since the original Alice got out of the rabbit hole. Of course, they really aren't crazy - they're telling the truth, but this truth is what got them tagged as insane in the first place. Now Alyssa fears the same will happen to her, especially since she hears the voice of insects talking to her. But she's determined to break this curse to save her mother Alison, so she goes down the rabbit hole again, and won't come back until she has accomplished her mission.<br><br>For starters, this tagging everyone in her family as crazy annoyed the hell out of me. Sure, if someone came to me to tell me a grasshopper told her I should take care of myself, I would be weirded out, but I wouldn't take it seriously. The person may have been making things up, or indeed, their mind in fact thinks a grasshopper did that, but is that a reason to apply 19th century treatments to them? No.<br><br>You see, <b>the portrayal of mental illness in this book makes me sick in so many levels.</b> Take a look at some things:<br><br><blockquote>Crazies like Alison - all they have are padded cells and blunted utensils. That's their normal.</blockquote><br><br>And not to mention Alyssa fears they're gonna use straitjackets on her too:<br><br><blockquote>Most of my makeup has been cried and rained off, leaving smudge tracks on my face. Now all I see is Alison. <b>But if I look deeper, it’s me wearing a straitjacket and an eel turban,</b> grimacing like the Cheshire Cat as I sip pot roast from a teacup.</blockquote><br><br>I know for a fact <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/society/2005/feb/02/mentalhealth.guardiansocietysupplement" rel="nofollow noopener">padded cells and straitjackets are not used anymore as a treatment</a>, so the mention of them as the treatment for someone that simply says bugs talk is extremely ignorant, and even if we ignored that, it's still exaggerated only to make everything more dramatic. As if someone who talks to insects was dangerous.<br><br>This is what annoyed me the most in this book. That alone would have settled my decision to rate this 1 star, but no, something else that made me even more angry had to be added. What's that, you ask? <b>It's an abusive romance.</b><br><br>Some people find cute when a guy is possessive over her girlfriend because "he wants the best for her." <b>I'm not one of those people.</b> Jeb gave me nauseas every time he appeared. He's not hot. He's not sweet. He's an asshole. Proof #1 is this:<br><br><blockquote>“Al.” His Adam’s apple moves as he swallows. “I want you to put a stop to this Hitch thing. Whatever’s going on, it’s not worth …” He pauses. “Losing an important part of you.”<br>Unbelievable. He thinks I’m such a prude, he won’t even say the word. “You mean my virginity?”<br>His neck flashes red. “You deserve better than some one-night thing. You’re the kind of girl who should have a commitment from a guy who actually cares. Okay?”</blockquote><br><br>Because not only does he have a girlfriend already and has done what he thinks Alyssa will do and worse with other girls, but he also thinks he can have the final word when it comes to Alyssa's virginity. Look, it's not his problem if she wants to screw a hundred guys. Why can he do it and not her? It doesn't matter she was lying. What bothers me is his attitude.<br><br>Being so possessive about Alyssa doesn't go only as far as her virginity, though. Remember the little synopsis I added at the beginning? About Alyssa being determined to break the curse? Well, this guy doesn't give a damn about that. He doesn't care Alyssa wants to save her mother (ignoring all the offensive and stupid things about the bad portrayal of mental illness). He only wants Alyssa for himself and won't let her go and try. And all that because of why? Because a guy - Morpheus - knows Alyssa from dreams.<br><br><blockquote>“No.” Jeb crosses my arms over my chest, then lifts me against one of the curtains on the wall so my feet dangle, pinning me like a butterfly to a corkboard. “We’re not going anywhere. That foaming freak thinks you stole those gloves. And now he knows your name. Very smooth, by the way.”</blockquote><br><br>Honestly, I don't understand why she's so attracted to him. She even fears him:<br><br><blockquote>Jeb’s supposed to meet me here. I’m dying to see him again <b>but at the same time nervous about how he’ll react to my decision to help Morpheus without talking things over with him first.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Look, if you feel you need to ask the permission of a guy for saving your mother, you should also feel there's something fishy going on there. Worse even if you worry what he'll do when he finds out you did something without asking him for that permission first. That will only lead to an unhealthy relationship in which he controls her and will probably get to the point of hitting her (not saying he did, by the way). What she said there is enough for cutting every connection she had to him.<br><br>Also, you can't just take all the elements in a book, make slight changes to their names and call that a retelling. Because yes, this book only feels as if the author mixed the two Alice books written by Carroll with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)" rel="nofollow noopener">that movie</a> and then she just switched some letters in the names of everything. For example, Rabid White is the White Rabbit, Queen Red is... well, it's obvious, and Humphrey is Humpty Dumpty.<br><br>Knowing all the possible options in which she could have made this a retelling, why did she have to go to the easiest and less imaginative one?<br><br>Then there's something else that bothered me. It's this line of the book:<br><br><blockquote>Pausing, he traces a finger along the door’s frame. “The last place she remembered having it was at your store. But she figured you would’ve contacted her if you’d found it. You didn’t see it, right?”<br>I push down the guilt nudging me. <b>“No. And I’m not her royal majesty’s purse keeper, FYI.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>I had said I liked the writing, and it's true, I liked the <i>descriptions</i>, but I don't think it's professional to type "FYI" instead of "for your information" in a book. It's even weirder because that was part of a dialogue. It's one thing to type that in text messages, but in dialogues? It just made me go like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457037829ra/18312515.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't think there's anything in this book that saves it from a 1-star rating, to be honest. And nothing can convince me to read the sequel, either, because 1) this could have perfectly been a standalone, and 2) I'm not interested anymore. I don't want to know anything about Jeb or the love triangle between Jeb, Alyssa and Morpheus, or this "curse." <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5186274.A_G__Howard" title="A.G. Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">A.G. Howard</a> has lost me. <b>I'm leaving this rabbit hole for good.</b><br><br>__________________________<br><br><b>Pre-review:</b><br><br>*Looks for <i>Splintered</i> by A.G. Howard*<br><br>*Sees this:*<br><br><blockquote>This family curse stretches back to her ancestor Alice Liddell, the real-life inspiration for Lewis Carroll’s <b><i>Alice’s Adventures in Wonderland</i></b>.</blockquote><br><br>*Immediatly adds to "to-read" shelf*<br><br>It's a retelling of <i>Alice In Wonderland</i>, guys! Of course I'm going to read it. Besides, <s>look at that cover. It could convinve <i>anyone</i> to read it</s> it sounds interesting and many people say it's good. So, yeah, I will read it...soon...when I find time...</span>
  <a data-text-id="7902944430664862653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_701241006" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/701241006" />
    <a title="Cassie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4143768-cassie"><img alt="Cassie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430358563p2/4143768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/701241006?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassie" href="/user/show/4143768-cassie">Cassie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4143768-cassie?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4143768-cassie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4143768-cassie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4143768-cassie?shelf=put-on-my-rantypants">put-on-my-rantypants</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer701241006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5334037491324760885">Ugh. Unlikable characters, plotting issues up the wazoo, derivative world-building (Tim Burton's Alice in Wonderland and Lewis Carroll's original book are NOT interchangeable, and it's really freaking obvious where the author rips off Burton wholesale)... No thanks. The audio had a much better narrator than the book merited.<br/><br/>Can the uber-possessive boyfriend thing stop now, please? Jeb, the main love interest (let's not kid ourselves that the love triangle was really a viable triangle in the firs</span>
  <span id="freeText5334037491324760885" style="display:none">Ugh. Unlikable characters, plotting issues up the wazoo, derivative world-building (Tim Burton's Alice in Wonderland and Lewis Carroll's original book are NOT interchangeable, and it's really freaking obvious where the author rips off Burton wholesale)... No thanks. The audio had a much better narrator than the book merited.<br /><br />Can the uber-possessive boyfriend thing stop now, please? Jeb, the main love interest (let's not kid ourselves that the love triangle was really a viable triangle in the first place, you knew she was always going to pick this douche), infantilizes and berates Alyssa at every turn. He appoints himself her knight and protector because she's too weak and fragile to make any of her own decisions and needs to be saved from herself. When we meet him, Alyssa is mad because he and her dad have mutually decided that she's too innocent and unworldly to attend an exchange program in London, even though Jeb is supposed to attend school in the city, too. Even though he and Alyssa are supposed to be besties, he's dating the mean girl whose teasing and rumor-mongering have made her a social outcast. WTF? And when Alyssa finally has the cojones to call him out on this, he explains that he only dated her mortal enemy to get Alyssa out of his system. Since Alyssa's a virgin (and this is a detail that's repeatedly expounded upon by Jeb), he decides he's too much of a bad boy for her and doesn't want to spoil her innocence. Um, let Alyssa make that choice herself, asshat.<br /><br />Morpheus wasn't much better, but at least he gave her the tools to empower herself even if he tried to harness that power to benefit himself. Also, it felt like he learned something through the whole experience. Even if he was a manipulative, lying, selfish jerk, he managed to make a sacrifice at the end. Jeb will never NOT be a jackwagon and ultimately is given no reason at all to change, but Morpheus actually exhibits a little bit of character growth. But once again, it's the losing party of the YA-mandated love triangle that actually treats the heroine as an equal. <br /><br />If, in the end, your heroine ends up being treated like a helpless damsel in distress by her ONE TWU WUV (like Alyssa is and characters like Bella and Luce and Nora before her), then can we finally do away with the pretense that she's empowered and strong? Because I'm sick of these kinds of off-kilter, unequal relationships being normalized. If Alyssa were empowered at all, she'd realize how much better off she is without EITHER of these pathetic excuses for love interests and demand a man that can complement her without coddling or condescending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5334037491324760885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_801161504" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/801161504" />
    <a title="Toni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24617462-toni"><img alt="Toni" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/801161504?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toni" href="/user/show/24617462-toni">Toni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781419706271" href="/book/show/15713147-splintered">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24617462-toni?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer801161504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11741378715808682144"><b>
  <i>"It's the Wonderland crew after a heavy dose of radiation poisoning."</i>
</b><br/><br/><i>Splintered</i> is a book you just have to stick with. My opinion of the book has drastically changed as soon as I hit the 100 pages mark. It transformed from a dull and tragically angsty story, to a twisted and beautiful one. <br/><br/>Alyssa Gardner is a great-great-great-grandaughter of Alice Liddel- the girl whose dreams inspired Lewis Carrol's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6799860.Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland' title='Alice's Adventures in Wonderland by Lewis Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alice's Adventures in Wonderland</a>. Every female in her family that was born since Alice, has</span>
  <span id="freeText11741378715808682144" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"It's the Wonderland crew after a heavy dose of radiation poisoning."</i>
</b><br><br><i>Splintered</i> is a book you just have to stick with. My opinion of the book has drastically changed as soon as I hit the 100 pages mark. It transformed from a dull and tragically angsty story, to a twisted and beautiful one. <br><br>Alyssa Gardner is a great-great-great-grandaughter of Alice Liddel- the girl whose dreams inspired Lewis Carrol's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6799860.Alice_s_Adventures_in_Wonderland" title="Alice's Adventures in Wonderland by Lewis Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice's Adventures in Wonderland</a>. Every female in her family that was born since Alice, has gone mad. Alyssa's mother is in an institution. Alyssa has a secret- <i>she can hear the thoughts of plants and bugs</i>. She has always believed she was going crazy too. Until now.<br>Suddenly there's a moth, that she keeps seeing everywhere. A moth connected to her past. She discovers that the madness in her family is a <i>curse</i>. In order to break it, she has to go down the rabbit hole and fix the wrongs done by Alice.<br><br>Wonderland though, is not exactly the land that we have all come to know.<br><br><b>The beginning sucked.</b> There were a few good things, but otherwise the before-wonderland part of the book just wasn't anything special. You had an annoying main character, that maybe wasn't as annoying alone, but when put together with the "noble and protective" Jeb, lost all nteresting qualities.<br><br><i>"My red T-shirt design: a bleeding heart wrapped in barbed wire. Might as well be an X-ray of my chest."</i><br><br>Spare me the woe-is-me crap Alyssa. Yes, you are tortured we get it.<br><br>Alyssa is constantly controlled by her father and her best friend slash <i>neighbour</i> Jeb. Her father doesn't let her dye her hair because she reminds him of her mother. And Jeb does shit like this:<br><br><i>"I was so psyched about the study-aboard program that allowed seniors to finish their final year of high school in London while getting college credit from one of the best art universities there. The very university Jeb's going to.<br>Since he's already received his scholarship and plans to move to London later this summer, Dad asked him to dinner a couple of weeks ago to talk about the program. I thought it was a great idea, that with Jeb in my corner I was as good as on a plane. <b>And then together they decided it wasn't the right time for me to go. They decided.</b>"</i><br><br>WHO DOES THAT? And then let's take into consideration that all he claims to want is to protect her, while also dating the girl who has always bullied her (and then of course the girl is portrayed as the only "villain"). I strongly disliked Jeb for the whole book, for various reasons.<br><br>What bothered me the most was that, yes Alyssa did get upset, but all was forgotten as soon as he reminded her of how much he <i>cared</i>. And his looks sure helped too.<br><br><b>BUT THEN...Wonderland happened.</b> And all was swell.<br><br>The way Howard created her own version of Wonderland, was something I haven't seen before. It connected the original story with a new darkness. <br><br>Howard's words and writing style are precious. Everything she writes is described so perfectly. You can feel the words. You can imagine being there.<br><br><b>"Their pointed ears and flowing hair sparkle, and their eyes are bulbous and metallic like a dragonfly's, as if they're wearing copper sunglasses. Wings flutter next to my cheek, milky white and furred with something resembling dandelion fuzz."</b><br><br>The plot of the book twists and turns. It's suprising and just a bunch of fun to read about. If you are familiar with the original fairy-tale this can be even more fun for you.<br><br>And then there's the star of the book. <i>Morpheus</i>.<br><br><b>
  <i>“He's a contradiction: taut magic coiled to strike, gentleness at war with severity, a tongue as sharp as a whip's edge, yet skin so soft he could be swathed in clouds.”</i>
</b><br><br>He is manipulative. He is flawed. He is <b>so damn interesting</b>. Morpheus seduces the reader into awe.<br><br>He is a wonderful anti-hero. And the sexual tension between him and Alyssa is unbelievable.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424817737ra/13805524.gif" width="430" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>All In All:</u> A fantastic retelling. It takes a bit to love, but you get there. I would definitely recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11741378715808682144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_488693500" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/488693500" />
    <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard"><img alt="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321462468p2/2216677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/488693500?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard">Cassi aka Snow White Haggard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=galleys">galleys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer488693500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9169101166938142074"><br/>Splintered is one of those books that has a great concept --the family of Alice Lidell (from Alice in Wonderland) is cursed with a special kinda crazy as a punishment for Alice's mistakes in Wonderland. Alyssa is only the latest in a line of women who hear the conversations of flowers and insects. Alyssa tries to hide the voices, killing the bugs and creating artwork while her mother wastes away in an insane asylum. Then she stumbles on a website about the rabbit hole and someone from Wonderland</span>
  <span id="freeText9169101166938142074" style="display:none"><br />Splintered is one of those books that has a great concept --the family of Alice Lidell (from Alice in Wonderland) is cursed with a special kinda crazy as a punishment for Alice's mistakes in Wonderland. Alyssa is only the latest in a line of women who hear the conversations of flowers and insects. Alyssa tries to hide the voices, killing the bugs and creating artwork while her mother wastes away in an insane asylum. Then she stumbles on a website about the rabbit hole and someone from Wonderland offers her a way to cure her families curse.<br /><br />Sounds interesting right? I know! Except the book completely lost it's own plot and instead turned into a poorly done paranormal romance without any real focus.<br /><br />Instead of focusing on Wonderland, which you know is kind of interesting, Alyssa is absorbed by Jeb--the best friend she's secretly in love with. All of their interactions and conversations just feel artificial. He constantly calls her "skater girl" as a pet name. Just a hint, taking your pet names from an Avril Lavine song is not cute.<br /><br />Everything feels forced. Jeb has a girlfriend who is less a character and more of an obstacle to the central relationship. She's a prop not a person. The moment Alyssa and Jeb pass into wonderland she's only brought up to create conflict (and this happens continually). There is drama, otherworldly creatures, pursuing armies, but the characters continually stop to argue about their relationship status.<br /><br />The arguments don't even make sense. Near the beginning before she goes into wonderland she tells Jeb finds out she's trying to get a fake passport from a guy who works at the skating rink (seriously those things have microchips now folks, it's not that easy) and he confronts her. She tells him to stay out of it. This is his eloquent and intelligent response.<br /><br /><i>"Out of what?" The pain in his voice rips me apart. "Stay out of your plan to hook up with some random loser, or stay out of your life." </i><br /><br />You may be wondering where he got the idea that Alyssa was going to hook up with a random loser. So am I. In the context of the story his accusions came out of nowhere. Alyssa is a virgin and there's no evidence pointing towards that that changing anytime soon. It's just an unnatural way to create another obstacle. Once they're in Wonderland he also accuses that a "perv lured you here via a magical website" showing his winning intellect once again.<br /><br />It was over-descriptive to the point of being purple prose, elaborating describing clothing hair and make-up, describing taste and scent in a way that didn't really make sense. The description was bothersome and at times downright confusing.<br /><br /><i>"The minute I'm free, I catch his thumb and nuzzle it. He tastes like grass and icing and all the flavors of Jeb, magnified." </i><br /><br />First off the nuzzling is weird. Second she's tasting him. Third, grass and icing? Really? Later he tastes like chocolate and salt. At least the salt makes sense, but chocolate? I know they say to use the five senses when writing description but it needs to make sense.<br /><br />Overall this book just did not work. I can't include every groan-worthy quote. The flaws, clumsy writing and shoddy storytelling overwhelm a good idea. Without the romance and some self control with descriptors this could actually be a good book. Unfortunately it's not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9169101166938142074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_424274106" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/424274106" />

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CkUCIqQVO17FYCJJvXbMQKSgqa6g1K39uqNbnvtX8AWIr8QdhRnE8J08lV3Qr9AO0F9cQFfL3aNKrdLdaC2oSA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Q4+dyKURGGckSTPU6lDzpAV4pcNfckgdkOqmaWwsCmbBZVv3hB3nyXwVhMCHie/qcYdQLahtOENg5C8q/1ZSKw==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText1877508674947843317" style="display:none">#1 New York Times and International bestselling Author of gothic / fantasy &amp; paranormal tales, mystical &amp; romantic with a side of horror. A.G.'s dark Alice in Wonderland inspired Splintered series has been published in over a dozen languages. <br /><br />Young adult, Adult, and literary romance. Repped by Jenny Bent.<br /><br />How A.G. Howard rates books on GoodReads:<br /><br />"I only rate or review books I enjoyed reading, and won't give any rating below 4 stars. Please don't consider every high rating a personal endorsement / recommendation from me. My ratings here are subjective to me as an individual. <br /><br />I don't rate books solely on style. Every writer's voice is individual and unique; I've come to respect this truth during my own personal journey. As long as a story takes me to another place and is well edited, I'm going to give it a good rating. And if, for some reason, a book doesn't entertain me or I don't finish it, I won't leave a rating or review at all. <br /><br />If you're considering a book I've reviewed/rated, be sure to read other reviews/ratings alongside mine to help you decide if it's a read you might enjoy personally.<br /><br />Happy book hunting!"<br /><br /></span>
